  <a href="#other_reviews" class="actionLinkLite votes">
      <span itemprop="ratingCount" title="603447" class="value-title">603,447 Ratings</span>
</a>  <span class="greyText"> · </span>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7648957399317437108">(Note: This edition is the Katherine Woods translation, not the recent Richard Howard translation, as the below description might suggest.)<br /><br />Antoine de Saint-Exupéry first published <em>The Little Prince</em> in 1943, only a year before his Lockheed P-38 vanished over the Mediterranean during a reconnaissance mission. More than a half century later, this fable of love and loneliness</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7648957399317437108">(Note: This edition is the Katherine Woods translation, not the recent Richard Howard translation, as the below description might suggest.)<br /><br />Antoine de Saint-Exupéry first published <em>The Little Prince</em> in 1943, only a year before his Lockheed P-38 vanished over the Mediterranean during a reconnaissance mission. More than a half century later, this fable of love and loneliness has lost none of its power. The narrator is a downed pilot in the Sahara Desert, frantically trying to repair his wrecked plane. His efforts are interrupted one day by the apparition of a little, well, prince, who asks him to draw a sheep. "In the face of an overpowering mystery, you don't dare disobey," the narrator recalls. "Absurd as it seemed, a thousand miles from all inhabited regions and in danger of death, I took a scrap of paper and a pen out of my pocket." And so begins their dialogue, which stretches the narrator's imagination in all sorts of surprising, childlike directions.<p> The Little Prince describes his journey from planet to planet, each tiny world populated by a single adult. It's a wonderfully inventive sequence, which evokes not only the great fairy tales but also such monuments of postmodern whimsy as Italo Calvino's <em>Invisible Cities</em>. And despite his tone of gentle bemusement, Saint-Exupéry pulls off some fine satiric touches, too. There's the king, for example, who commands the Little Prince to function as a one-man (or one-boy) judiciary: </p><blockquote>I have good reason to believe that there is an old rat living somewhere on my planet. I hear him at night. You could judge that old rat. From time to time you will condemn him to death. That way his life will depend on your justice. But you'll pardon him each time for economy's sake. There's only one rat. </blockquote> The author pokes similar fun at a businessman, a geographer, and a lamplighter, all of whom signify some futile aspect of adult existence. Yet his tale is ultimately a tender one--a heartfelt exposition of sadness and solitude, which never turns into <em>Peter Pan</em>-style treacle. Such delicacy of tone can present real headaches for a translator, and in her 1943 translation, Katherine Woods sometimes wandered off the mark, giving the text a slightly wooden or didactic accent. Happily, Richard Howard (who did a fine nip-and-tuck job on Stendhal's <em>The Charterhouse of Parma</em> in 1999) has streamlined and simplified to wonderful effect. The result is a new and improved version of an indestructible classic, which also restores the original artwork to full color. "Trying to be witty," we're told at one point, "leads to lying, more or less." But Saint-Exupéry's drawings offer a handy rebuttal: they're fresh, funny, and like the book itself, rigorously truthful. <em>--James Marcus</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7648957399317437108">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

</div>

<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/35361568-jorge-l" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/35361568-jorge-l">Jorge L.</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">That's a hard question to answer. Technically, this book is suitable for children as young as 6 years old but I doubt that most would completely<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">That's a hard question to answer. Technically, this book is suitable for children as young as 6 years old but I doubt that most would completely understand it at that age. One of my professors once told me that this book should be read 3 times in one's life: as a child, as a young adult and as an older adult. I think he said so because as we grow older our perspective changes, and thus we become able to appreciate things in different ways.<br />I'd say that teenagers and adults would enjoy this book the most.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class="communityQuestionAndAnswer">
<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/250979-many-reviewers-say-this-book-has-deep">Many reviewers say this book has deep meanings, but not one person has indicated what those deep meanings are. What do you think the author was trying to tell the reader?</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_250979" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/250979?resource_type=CommunityQuestion" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_community_question_250979"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F728232.The_Little_Prince" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp">
<a href="/questions/250979-many-reviewers-say-this-book-has-deep">one year ago</a>
</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionPermalink">
<a href="/questions/250979-many-reviewers-say-this-book-has-deep">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/14804680-sandra" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/14804680-sandra">Sandra</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are many themes in the book: (e.g., People tend to become less creative and imaginative as they grow into adulthood. Most adults are preoccupied<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are many themes in the book: (e.g., People tend to become less creative and imaginative as they grow into adulthood. Most adults are preoccupied with things of little real value.) For me, one of the most important themes is that we give purpose and meaning to our lives through the relationships (especially of love and friendship) we form. The Little Prince's rose is unique and more important to him than all the other roses because he cares for it and takes responsibility for it. After he tames (a metaphor for forming a relationship) the fox, it, likewise, becomes different to him from all the other foxes, and he feels responsible for it.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerFooter">

</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17177396756171041592">The next asteroid the Little Prince came to was inhabited by a Quiz Addict. He sat hunched in front of his laptop, and barely looked up when the Little Prince greeted him. There was nowhere else to sit, since the whole asteroid was covered in books.<br /><br />"Good morning!" said the Little Prince.<br /><br />"I'm sorry, I don't have time to talk to you," said the Quiz Addict. "I am very busy. Wait. In <em>Twilight</em>, what color was Edward's car?"<br /><br />"I don't know," said the Little Prince. "I have never read this book <em>Twilight</em>.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17177396756171041592">The next asteroid the Little Prince came to was inhabited by a Quiz Addict. He sat hunched in front of his laptop, and barely looked up when the Little Prince greeted him. There was nowhere else to sit, since the whole asteroid was covered in books.<br /><br />"Good morning!" said the Little Prince.<br /><br />"I'm sorry, I don't have time to talk to you," said the Quiz Addict. "I am very busy. Wait. In <em>Twilight</em>, what color was Edward's car?"<br /><br />"I don't know," said the Little Prince. "I have never read this book <em>Twilight</em>."<br /><br />"I think it was blue," said the man. "Damn! I was wrong. Silver. In <em>Twilight</em>, who joined the Cullen family first?"<br /><br />"I told you," said the Little Prince, "that I haven't read this book. But it must be an interesting book if you answer questions about it all day long. I would very much like to read it."<br /><br />"It is the stupidest book ever written!" said the man.<br /><br />"Then why do you answer questions about it all day long?" asked the Little Prince.<br /><br />"Because if I don't," sighed the man, "then my friend on asteroid B451 will get ahead of me. "He has read the whole series. Luckily, he hasn't read <em>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</em>."<br /><br />"When you have finished the Quiz," asked the Little Prince, "I hope you will be able to read some of these books you have around you? I notice that you have had <em>Atonement</em> on your to-read list for the last six months."<br /><br />"It is a Never-Ending Quiz," answered the man. "In <em>Twilight</em>, what color was Edward's car?"<br /><br />"I believe you said silver?" answered the Little Prince politely.<br /><br />"Thank you," muttered the man. "Yes! You were right. I should have known that."<br /><br />"I'm sorry, I must be going," said the Little Prince. And he went on his way, thinking that grown-ups were very, very, very strange.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17177396756171041592">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_101065949">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101065949" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" class="left imgcol" title="Nataliya"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395089173p2/3672777.jpg" alt="Nataliya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/101065949?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" class="user" title="Nataliya">Nataliya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=my-childhood-bookshelves" class="actionLinkLite">my-childhood-bookshelves</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=excellent-reads" class="actionLinkLite">excellent-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter" class="actionLinkLite">for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2014-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=books-from-childhood-revisited" class="actionLinkLite">books-from-childhood-revisited</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101065949">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1982841603749830293"><br /><strong>*** For those who somehow have no idea about what happens in <em>The Little Prince</em> or cannot figure it out at a reasonable spot in the book, here is a warning - <u>THERE WILL BE,</u> as much as I hate applying this term to this incredibly famous classic that does not rely on <em>Aha!</em> moments to keep the readers' attention, <u>SPOILERS!</u> ****</strong><br /><br /><br />-----------<br /><br /><br /><em>'You do understand that the Little Prince died?'</em> my mother asked as carefully and gently as only adults who know that loss of innocence can be crushing but is brutal</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1982841603749830293"><br /><strong>*** For those who somehow have no idea about what happens in <em>The Little Prince</em> or cannot figure it out at a reasonable spot in the book, here is a warning - <u>THERE WILL BE,</u> as much as I hate applying this term to this incredibly famous classic that does not rely on <em>Aha!</em> moments to keep the readers' attention, <u>SPOILERS!</u> ****</strong><br /><br /><br />-----------<br /><br /><br /><em>'You do understand that the Little Prince died?'</em> my mother asked as carefully and gently as only adults who know that loss of innocence can be crushing but is brutally necessary can do.<br /><br /><em>'No, he didn't. He went back to his home planet and that stupid rose. It says so right here,</em>' I replied with the comforting stubbornness of an eight-year-old.<br /><br />Later that night, I quietly reread the book and the sad truth clicked, and so did the belated thought that<strong> for all the gentle berating of adults in it, this strange and beautiful book was written by one of them and definitely for them, and not for me, and by luring me in with the beautiful pictures it pushed me just a bit further on the inevitable road to adulthood.</strong><br /><br />Or so I see now.<br /><br />Back then, I decided to read the author's biography instead as a distraction from the thoughts that were trying to be a bit more grown-up than my heart cared for - I was the odd kid of a literature teacher mother, after all - just to learn that just after writing this book, Antoine de Saint Exupery died when flying his plane in a war to liberate his country, killed by adults who played a game of war, too dangerous and cruel. And that finally made me cry. <br /><br />And then I went back to the simple security of childhood.<br /><br /><br /><img width="400" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392675929i/8593073.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Then I grew up, inevitably, like most of us do. I learned to do my fair share of 'matters of consequence'.</strong> I learned the painful understanding of why certain vain but naive roses can hold such sad power over our hearts. I learned the comfort and longing of nostalgia, the fear of the crushing burden of loneliness, the understanding of fragile beauty of the world that can be so easily taken away at any moment. I became a grown-up, and I have to learn to reconcile my inner child with my outer age.<blockquote>
  <em>"In the course of this life I have had a great many encounters with a great many people who have been concerned with matters of consequence. I have lived a great deal among grown-ups. I have seen them intimately, close at hand. And that hasn't much improved my opinion of them."</em>
</blockquote>Now, reading this intensely lyrical and mesmerizing book written by an ailing middle-aged adult far away from the country he loved in the middle of war-torn years, I am confronted with emotions that ruthlessly hurt, hidden in the deceiving simplicity of a (supposedly) children's story just like an elephant was hidden inside a boa constrictor - or was it simply a hat all along? - in the opening paragraphs of this book. I sigh and tear up, and try to resist the urge to pick up the golden-haired child that never stopped until he got answers to his questions and carry him away into safety. But I can't. <strong>Because if I do so, there will never be 500 billion bells in the stars, and we will never wonder whether the rose is still alive - and it needs to be, because we are responsible for those we have tamed.</strong><blockquote>
  <em>"But I was not reassured. I remembered the fox. One runs the risk of weeping a little, if one lets himself be tamed."</em>
</blockquote>This is not a book for children. It's for adults who remember being children and feel nostalgia for the simple comfort of childhood innocence but know they can never go back to it.<strong> Because they have met their Roses, and Foxes, and drank from a well with a rusty handle in the desert, and learned that a few thorns may not stand against the claws of a tiger. </strong>Unlike the Little Prince, they can no longer go back - but they can look at the night starry sky and laugh, and imagine that they hear an answering clear laughter.<blockquote>
  <em>"In certain more important details I shall make mistakes, also. But that is something that will not be my fault. My friend never explained anything to me. He thought, perhaps, that I was like himself. But I, alas, do not know how to see sheep through t he walls of boxes. Perhaps I am a little like the grown-ups. I have had to grow old."<br /><br /><img width="320" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392675213i/8592936.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>'What makes the desert beautiful,' said the little prince, 'is that somewhere it hides a well.'</strong></em>
</blockquote></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1982841603749830293">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/21285369?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 29, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/231873-erin" class="user" title="Erin ">Erin </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer21285369">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2089737428917580718">We are all children in adults bodies. Yes we are, don't think we aren't for one moment. The fact that we WERE, indeed, children, is a huge part of each of us. It is possible to shed a few appreciative tears on every page of this book if you entertain the thought that the pilot IS The Little Prince. Maybe you won't think that--maybe you'll have your own take on the book---that's the magic about it. This book is translated to English from French. If you understand and/or appreciate French, the del</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2089737428917580718">We are all children in adults bodies. Yes we are, don't think we aren't for one moment. The fact that we WERE, indeed, children, is a huge part of each of us. It is possible to shed a few appreciative tears on every page of this book if you entertain the thought that the pilot IS The Little Prince. Maybe you won't think that--maybe you'll have your own take on the book---that's the magic about it. This book is translated to English from French. If you understand and/or appreciate French, the deliciousness of that fact can affect you in addition to the sweet storyline itself. The book won't even take you a whole day to read. Consider honoring the Little You that still remains, and resides within you, and read this 'salute' to childhood, to innocence, and to you. It just takes a 'Little' imagination and bravery.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_116924600">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116924600" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" alt="Stephen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/116924600?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="user" title="Stephen">Stephen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1930-1953" class="actionLinkLite">1930-1953</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer116924600">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13372550304849649277">A <strong>"Daddy/Daughter nighttime reading hour"</strong> review<br /><br />This was a <strong>toughy</strong> for me to review. I wasn't sure of the best perspective from which to provide comments so as to be of assistance to my fellow readers since this is a children's book (rather than YA which would be reviewed purely on its own merits). After a short session of "what should I do," I bravely decided to <strong>punt</strong>, figuring that there are already more than enough excellent reviews of this without my clogging up the cyber arteries with another</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13372550304849649277">A <strong>"Daddy/Daughter nighttime reading hour"</strong> review<br /><br />This was a <strong>toughy</strong> for me to review. I wasn't sure of the best perspective from which to provide comments so as to be of assistance to my fellow readers since this is a children's book (rather than YA which would be reviewed purely on its own merits). After a short session of "what should I do," I bravely decided to <strong>punt</strong>, figuring that there are already more than enough excellent reviews of this without my clogging up the cyber arteries with another one. Therefore, I decided simply to share my experience of reading/listening to the book with my daughter along with a couple of thoughts on the concepts discussed in the story and hope that you can take something useful from it. <br /><br />So as part of our nightly routine, my youngest daughter, Sydney, and I have daddy/princess read time. The other night, she and I listened to the audio version of <em>The Little Prince</em> while we read along with a copy of the book. As usual, it was an <strong>AMAZING</strong> experience. I am convinced that I learn more about the stories we read from her and her reactions to the narrative than she does from me...and I love it. <br /><br />It's only a two hour audio (86 pages) and yet the two of us spent close to 4 hours listening and talking about the various chapters in the story (plus a brief 15 minute break for Mom to give her a bath while Dad helped big sister Kenzie with her math homework). Sydney had all kinds of questions (some just hysterically funny in how much sense they made from a kid-centric view of the world). We would stop the story after each planet or character to talk about what she thought the story meant and what messages the story was trying to deliver. <br />For those of you with children, you know how wonderful this can be and I was on the <strong>ninth cloud</strong> watching my little girl ponder over the book. <br /><br />From this perspective, the story was perfect and deserves an easy 5 stars. However, since it's not very helpful to rate a book based on that kind of non-transferable experience, I didn't want to rely solely on that for its final rating. <br /><br />After explaining to Syd the goodreads star system, she would give this 4 stars as she really liked the British accent of the narrator and the crazy adventures the Prince experiences on the various planets. BTW, from Sydney's point of view, 4 stars is the absolute ceiling for any book dealing with <strong>ickies</strong> like boys and this would easily earn 5 stars had the story been called the <strong>"The Little Princess."</strong> Princes are still second class citizens at this stage in her life...and Dad is oh, oh, OH so perfectly fine with that).<br /><br />For me, looking at this <strong>sans</strong> Sydney, I liked it but was not smitten with it enough to go higher than 3 stars. The story is well written and has something to say about the human condition and how people spend too much of their lives focusing on the wrong things and not enough time enjoying where they are. A nice message and one I was happy to expose Sydney to, but I was not always enamored with the path the author took to get there. <br /><br />Overall, a good read on its own and a potentially a great experience if shared with your children...as most things in life are. <br /><br />3.5 stars. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13372550304849649277">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1093290802">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093290802" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/665584-alejandro" class="left imgcol" title="Alejandro"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" alt="Alejandro" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1093290802?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/665584-alejandro" class="user" title="Alejandro">Alejandro</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=religion" class="actionLinkLite">religion</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=politics" class="actionLinkLite">politics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=magic" class="actionLinkLite">magic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel" class="actionLinkLite">novel</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1093290802">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer723090552584860906"><strong> <u>Beautiful reading!</u> </strong><br /><br /><br /><strong> <u>WHEN A ROSE IS NOT A ROSE</u> </strong><br /><br /><strong> <em>It is only with the heart that one can see rightly; what is essential is invisible to the eye.</em> </strong><br /><br />I plan to read <em>The Little Prince</em> since many time ago, and I was aware that it was a quick reading, but still I hadn’t do it yet, until now.<br /><br />I went to the cinema theaters and I watched the new animated film about it, and while I hadn’t read the book, I watched the film and I loved it. I was aware that it wasn’t an exact adaptation per se, and then I knew th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText723090552584860906"><strong>
  <u>Beautiful reading!</u>
</strong><br /><br /><br /><strong>
  <u>WHEN A ROSE IS NOT A ROSE</u>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>It is only with the heart that one can see rightly; what is essential is invisible to the eye.</em>
</strong><br /><br />I plan to read <em>The Little Prince</em> since many time ago, and I was aware that it was a quick reading, but still I hadn’t do it yet, until now.<br /><br />I went to the cinema theaters and I watched the new animated film about it, and while I hadn’t read the book, I watched the film and I loved it. I was aware that it wasn’t an exact adaptation per se, and then I knew that it was about time to read the book. <br /><br />It was a quick reading, it took me like a couple of hours. Wonderful book.<br /><em>The Little Prince</em> is a metaphorical and surrealist journey where a rose isn’t necessarily a rose, a fox isn’t always a fox, a small planet isn’t a small planet all the time...<br /><br />All those things and more that you can find in the book, they will be whatever you need to be. You just need to recognize what will be the rose, what will be the fox, what will be the small planet...<br /><br />And then, and only then you will be able to realice the power behind of this cute little book.<br /><br /><br /><strong>
  <u>HIDDEN THINGS</u>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>What makes the desert beautiful,... ...,is that somewhere it hides a well...</em>
</strong><br /><br />Also, a hidden wonder about this book is that you not only need to realice what things in your own life to interchange with the ones in the Little Prince’s journey, but moreover, you need to “see” with your heart and being able to find the “well” in every “desert”.<br /><br />Sometimes isn’t easy, and I guess that there will be moments when those deserts are truly dry, maybe there was a well some time ago, but it’s long gone. But only you, if you are careful and “observant” with your heart, you will be able to make the difference.<br /><br />At plain sight, your eyes can deceive you about what it’s in front of you, but if you learn to “watch” with your heart, rarely you will be fooled about it.<br /><br />So, not matter if you are in a desert or a little planet (most likely an asteroid), be prepared to take flight and be ready with paper and a pencil, since who knows? Maybe the Little Prince will need you to draw something beyond the evident...<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="723090552584860906">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who know a sated boa constrictor is *not* a hat</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/69506-anne?shelf=for-kids-and-ubercool-grownups" class="actionLinkLite">for-kids-and-ubercool-grownups</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1141751">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9411170815018264413">There's a huge place in my heart for this little world-in-a-book; I read it first when I was wee, again many times since. A review won't do it justice, so I'll quote one of my favorite passages and risk sentimentality:<br />---<br />"Nothing is perfect," sighed the fox.<br />But he came back to his idea.<br />"My life's very monotonous," he said. "I hunt chickens; men hunt me.<br />All chickens are just alike, and all the men are just alike.<br />And in consequence, I am a little bored.<br />But if you tame me, it'll be as if the sun ca</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9411170815018264413">There's a huge place in my heart for this little world-in-a-book; I read it first when I was wee, again many times since. A review won't do it justice, so I'll quote one of my favorite passages and risk sentimentality:<br />---<br />"Nothing is perfect," sighed the fox.<br />But he came back to his idea.<br />"My life's very monotonous," he said. "I hunt chickens; men hunt me.<br />All chickens are just alike, and all the men are just alike.<br />And in consequence, I am a little bored.<br />But if you tame me, it'll be as if the sun came to shine on my life.<br />I shall know the sound of a step that'll be different from all the others.<br />Other steps send me hurrying back underneath the ground.<br />Yours will call me, like music out of my burrow.<br />And then look: you see the grain-fields down yonder?<br />I do not eat bread. Wheat is of no use to me.<br />The wheat fields have nothing to say to me. And that is sad.<br />But you have hair that is the color of gold.<br />Think how wonderful that will be when you have tamed me!<br />The grain, which is also golden, will bring me back the thought of you.<br />And I shall love to listen to the wind in the wheat…"<br />---<br /><br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/4686064-rajat-ubhaykar" class="left imgcol" title="Rajat Ubhaykar"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1352663955p2/4686064.jpg" alt="Rajat Ubhaykar" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/249255934?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4686064-rajat-ubhaykar" class="user" title="Rajat Ubhaykar">Rajat Ubhaykar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer249255934">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer541883351402231524">Written as a children's book, I find myself unable to pin down firmly as to what makes The Little Prince such a universally likeable book, be it children or grown-ups. What makes it the Hotel California of literature? <br /><br />Is it because most grown-ups secretly love being treated like kids? I think as a grown-up you ought to know better than that. Grown-ups like to be petted around now and then in jest, but that's the end of it. Often, when grown-ups are indeed treated like kids and they're not in the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText541883351402231524">Written as a children's book, I find myself unable to pin down firmly as to what makes The Little Prince such a universally likeable book, be it children or grown-ups. What makes it the Hotel California of literature? <br /><br />Is it because most grown-ups secretly love being treated like kids? I think as a grown-up you ought to know better than that. Grown-ups like to be petted around now and then in jest, but that's the end of it. Often, when grown-ups are indeed treated like kids and they're not in the mood, there is a tiny matchstick inside each one of them, an insecure ego which flares up angrily like it has been wildly struck against a matchbox. In my experience, grown ups like to be taken very seriously. Very very seriously. <br /><br />Is it the clear, simple language? No, it can't be just that. There have been books that have been written with clarity and have been criticized by pedants and pontificating bores for their simplicity. Grown ups like to feel wise and learned by having claimed to read complicated texts that engaged them at an 'intellectual' level. They don't like important things being pointed out to them in simple language, after all they're the know-it-all grown-ups and don't need anybody patronizing them. <br /><br />Is it because the book is so short and grown-ups are always keen on finishing books real quick? No, it can't be just that either. I know grown-ups who believe that a good book, like a well-mixed drink, must be held between the fingers and tended to lovingly at length to let it get to your head.<br /><br />Is it the timeless lessons that the book cushions behind layers of delightful story-telling? Is it the sense of wonder that the book inspires in the most cynical, world-weary adult, if not for posterity then for a day or an hour? I don't know, could be, could be. Worthy contenders they are, but I think I'm not still not home. <br /><br />If I had to lay a bet on it, I'd say everyone adores The Little Prince because we are tired of meeting people from Earth everyday who speak the same dry language of numbers and would love to encounter a sunset-loving, wise prince from the room-sized planet of Asteroid B-612 who talks animatedly about butterflies, baobabs and volcanoes to the child inside us that we've buried long ago underneath the grey tomb of grown-up babble. <br /><br />Kurt Vonnegut once expressed how laughable a critic taking himself too seriously is in these memorable words, <br /><em>"Any reviewer who expresses rage and loathing for a novel is preposterous. He or she is like a person who has put on full armor and attacked a hot fudge sundae.”</em> <br /><br />That is exactly how ridiculous critics who despise The Little Prince are. For The Little Prince is that hot fudge sundae garnished with generous toppings of lost innocence, shared loneliness, deliciously recycled perspective and lessons worth repeating to yourself to keep from succumbing to the unsavoury, contagious disease of adulthood. <br /><br />To make your job easier, here are some lessons from the book worth remembering and repeating:<br /><br /><em>"It is only with the heart that one can see rightly. What is essential is invisible to the eye."<br /><br />"People have forgotten this truth," the fox said. "But you mustn’t forget it. You become responsible forever for what you’ve tamed."<br /><br />"One only understands the things that one tames,' said the fox. 'Men have no more time to understand anything. They buy things all ready made at the shops. But there is no shop anywhere where one can buy friendship, and so men have no friends any more. If you want a friend, tame me."<br /><br />"“Grown-ups love figures... When you tell them you've made a new friend they never ask you any questions about essential matters. They never say to you "What does his voice sound like? What games does he love best? Does he collect butterflies? " Instead they demand "How old is he? How much does he weigh? How much money does his father make? " Only from these figures do they think they have learned anything about him.”</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="541883351402231524">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/208492752?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma" class="user" title="Nandakishore Varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/578618.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780749707231" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6237864-nandakishore-varma?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer208492752">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2449175209285065906">I have read only three books which I felt were magical: <a title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a>, <a title="To Kill a Mockingbird by Harper Lee" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2657.To_Kill_a_Mockingbird">To Kill a Mockingbird</a> and this one. However, what separates this from the other two is that this is a book for all ages.<br /><br />There was a magazine called "Imprint" (now defunct) during my childhood, in India. It used to publish literary articles and stories. My father got official copies and he brought them home regularly. One issue contained this story, and he gave it to me for reading. I was maybe 10-12 at that ti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2449175209285065906">I have read only three books which I felt were magical: <a title="One Hundred Years of Solitude by Gabriel Garcí­a Márquez" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/320.One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a>, <a title="To Kill a Mockingbird by Harper Lee" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2657.To_Kill_a_Mockingbird">To Kill a Mockingbird</a> and this one. However, what separates this from the other two is that this is a book for all ages.<br /><br />There was a magazine called "Imprint" (now defunct) during my childhood, in India. It used to publish literary articles and stories. My father got official copies and he brought them home regularly. One issue contained this story, and he gave it to me for reading. I was maybe 10-12 at that time.<br /><br />It left an indelible impression on my mind: I was sad for the little prince and his proud rose, and constantly worried whether the goat would eat it. I chuckled at the silly grownups on the various planets, following their inane pursuits. I was sad when the fox and the prince had to separate, after he had tamed it. And I broke down and cried at the end.<br /><br />I read this book again after a long time... and suddenly realised that I had become one of those adults on the asteroids. I was still sad after reading it-but now the sorrow had a deeper meaning. It was the death of childhood that I was reading about.<br /><br />This book is an absolute treasure.<br /><br /><u>Postscript</u><br /><br />July 22, 2015 - I gave this book to my son a couple of days back. Hopefully he'll read it - he has yet to fully transform into a silly grown-up.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2449175209285065906">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a href="/review/show/1072269?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 06, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/77009-laurel" class="user" title="Laurel">Laurel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/70720.Le_Petit_Prince" title="Paperback 9783125971400" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1072269">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15986563551256273930">It was the first time in quite a while that I'd seen my uncle. He had crossed the country to visit us. When he reached our house, he hugged and kissed us all, then pulled out the English version of this book.<br />"This is for you," he said, "and on the next starry night, I'm going to read it to you."<br />I gave him a puzzled look.<br />He explained, "you have to read this on a night when you can see the stars. Don't worry, you'll understand."<br /><br />The starry night came, and we settled in for a few hours of reading. A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15986563551256273930">It was the first time in quite a while that I'd seen my uncle. He had crossed the country to visit us. When he reached our house, he hugged and kissed us all, then pulled out the English version of this book.<br />"This is for you," he said, "and on the next starry night, I'm going to read it to you."<br />I gave him a puzzled look.<br />He explained, "you have to read this on a night when you can see the stars. Don't worry, you'll understand."<br /><br />The starry night came, and we settled in for a few hours of reading. As he finished the last page, we became silent. Then we stood up, went outside, and gazed up at the twinkling laughter of the little prince.<br /><br /><br />I've been meaning to read the French version for a long time, and I've finally dedicated myself to reading it when I can spare a few minutes. So far, it is just as good as its English counterpart. <br /><br />Everyone, and I mean everyone, needs to read this book. It may break your heart a little bit.<br /><br /><em>Voici mon secret. Il est très simple: on ne voit bien qu'avec le coeur. L'essentiel est invisible pour les yeux.</em><br /><br />-Antoine de Saint-Exupéry<br /><em>Le Petit Prince</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15986563551256273930">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/30706760-afshar" class="left imgcol" title="Afshar"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449347155p2/30706760.jpg" alt="Afshar" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/941736281?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 18, 2015</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_51910831">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51910831" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="left imgcol" title="K.D. Absolutely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449978413p2/2156200.jpg" alt="K.D. Absolutely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/51910831?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="user" title="K.D. Absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jillian</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=1001-core" class="actionLinkLite">1001-core</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501" class="actionLinkLite">501</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer51910831">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6153308848223921219"><strong>Review After Re-Reading - February 9, 2012</strong><br /><br />Rating: 3 stars! <br /><br />Although I still liked it, I have to lower the rating by two stars because:<blockquote>1. The book is really intended for children as it is very whimsical and illogical. We husbands cannot give an empty wallet to our wives and tell them that there is our salary inside and expect them to be happy. <em>Honey, here is my wallet, what is essential is invisible to your eyes!</em><br /><br />2. Saint-Ex contradicted himself so several times via his characters. For example, he</blockquote></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6153308848223921219"><strong>Review After Re-Reading - February 9, 2012</strong><br /><br />Rating: 3 stars! <br /><br />Although I still liked it, I have to lower the rating by two stars because:<blockquote>1. The book is really intended for children as it is very whimsical and illogical. We husbands cannot give an empty wallet to our wives and tell them that there is our salary inside and expect them to be happy. <em>Honey, here is my wallet, what is essential is invisible to your eyes!</em><br /><br />2. Saint-Ex contradicted himself so several times via his characters. For example, he left his small planet because he was unhappy with his rose. So, why did he not go back right away since he was able to do so via the migratory birds. Why did he have to let the snake bite him for his soul to go back to his planet? (Ok. This is just my interpretation). <br /><br />3. This just cannot be in the same rank together with my other top favorite books like Gabriel Garcia Marquez's <em>One Hundred Years of Solitude</em>, Doris Lessing's <em>The Golden Notebook</em> or Vladimir Nabokov's <em>Lolita</em>. Although I admire Saint-Ex, his works (I read two including this) cannot hold candle to the works of these 3 favorite authors of mine. I know this is debatable but it's just a matter of preference.</blockquote> However, this is still my favorite <em>children's</em> book along with E. B. White's <em>Charlotte's Web.</em><br /><br />To took me so long to figure this for myself: sometimes we love books not because they are really good but because of the memories associated with them. I think that's the main reason why I rated this 5 stars when I joined Goodreads.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. While re-reading, this book still put a smile on my face. I just figured today that the reason was the memories. Had this been my first time to read this, I would have rated this, for whatever it's worth, also with 3-stars (I like this!)<br /><br /><br /><strong>Original Review in March 2009 when I joined Goodreads</strong><br /><br />Rating: 5 stars!<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>First read in full sometime in 1992 when I was in college</strong>
</em><br /><br />I will not be ashamed to admit that this is my favorite novel of them all. I read this when I was young and I can still recall the detail of each encounter or planet where he went. Who can also forget the famous line: "What is essential is invisible to the eye"? Even Ruffa Gutierrez quoted this line when she competed in Miss World beauty pageant a couple of decades ago. For all its ethereal beauty, meaningful lines and timeless messages, this novel is one that I will read again before I die and I hope Jillian will encourage her kids in the future to read this too.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6153308848223921219">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2990642-rowena?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer495145421">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1112323598218350212">Oh this book! The Little Prince has been my faithful and trusted friend since I was a child. It's amazing how differently I looked at the book as an innocent 9 year old to the adult who I am now. The simple truths in this book are amazing, I could quote them for days and days. They are very philosophical and even though they are often over-quoted, it doesn't make them less true. The illustrations are simple. I re-read this book at least once a year to remind myself to be as inquisitive as a chil</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1112323598218350212">Oh this book! The Little Prince has been my faithful and trusted friend since I was a child. It's amazing how differently I looked at the book as an innocent 9 year old to the adult who I am now. The simple truths in this book are amazing, I could quote them for days and days. They are very philosophical and even though they are often over-quoted, it doesn't make them less true. The illustrations are simple. I re-read this book at least once a year to remind myself to be as inquisitive as a child. Having read both the English and French versions, I can say I love them equally in both languages.<br /><br />This book will always have a special place on my bookshelf.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1341273075">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1341273075" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/36859595-nishat" class="left imgcol" title="Nishat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447837060p2/36859595.jpg" alt="Nishat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1341273075?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/36859595-nishat" class="user" title="Nishat">Nishat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All the grown-ups who remember being children</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=heart-touching" class="actionLinkLite">heart-touching</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=delicate-as-poetry" class="actionLinkLite">delicate-as-poetry</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=joyous" class="actionLinkLite">joyous</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read" class="actionLinkLite">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/36859595-nishat?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1341273075">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8483837741465688502"><em>"Only the children know what they are looking for"</em><br /><br />A child can be mysterious. He doesn't know much. The time that is offered to him, is the time he passes lavishly. Memories that he make, are the memories that will wound and comfort him later in his life. Secrets that he lock in his sweet, stubborn heart, are bits of the unattainable truth that he will search for later. Because a child knows enough. Because he knows what he wants.<br /><br /><em>"Wait for a time, exactly under the star. Then, if a little man app</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8483837741465688502"><em>"Only the children know what they are looking for"</em><br /><br />A child can be mysterious. He doesn't know much. The time that is offered to him, is the time he passes lavishly. Memories that he make, are the memories that will wound and comfort him later in his life. Secrets that he lock in his sweet, stubborn heart, are bits of the unattainable truth that he will search for later. Because a child knows enough. Because he knows what he wants.<br /><br /><em>"Wait for a time, exactly under the star. Then, if a little man appears who laughs, who has golden hair and who refuses to answer questions, you will know who he is."</em><br /><br />I know. He is The Little Prince who owns the most mesmerizing story of liveliness and loneliness, shaped and drawn by the very talented Antoine de Saint-Exupéry. And he has landed on Earth from far away only to share the charming tale of his love and loss that will make us laugh and weep years later.<br /><br />The narrator who crashes in the desert as the author, Saint-Exupéry once did, believes that the grown-ups, in his view, can’t really see past the surface of things. And miraculously he meets a tiny boy in the desert wandering alone, referred as The Little Prince who shares the same perspective. Together they dissect the very human nature which is enough I believe, to shake the readers who are all too wrapped up in their own affairs and make them to contemplate on their priorities. <br /><br /><em>"It is such a secret place, the land of tears."</em><br /><br />The little prince lives in a very small place, Asteroid B-612. He has 3 volcanoes to clean &amp; a breathtaking sunset to watch everyday. He has a flower that is completely unique in his world &amp; he loves her dearly. But the flower's vanity hurt him deeply which led the prince to set off to a new journey with a scarred heart to the unseen. And as he travels other planets, he finds each one inhabited by an odd, unreasonable man, until the prince comes to Earth where he learns the importance of bonds that we make and the stories we tell ourselves to live on. And as the pages turn, an unforgettable tale of affection, friendship and the loss of innocence unfolds itself slowly.<br /><br /><em>"It is only with the heart that one can see rightly; what is essential is invisible to the eye."</em><br /><br />Who is to tell a child that in stars dead do not linger? Who is to tell a child that he does not know what he thinks he does? We live in a shell. Only when you pierce through that shell that we put proudly on, you will know the truth. Because only then the heart will have eyes and the heart will see. Because only then a mediocre poem of a hard working poet or a sunk ship of dead bodies, will be cared for. <br /><br />Because what matters most is always bigger than us !<br /><br />This is not a children's book clearly. The flower represents the author's Salvadoran wife whom he cheated on several times, but yet could not leave or forget. Because in other flowers, he found merely emptiness, but in her he smelled of love and dedication that he solely owned. The grasping baobab trees represented Nazism attempting to destroy the planet. The little prince is widely believed to be the author's own self.<br /><br /><em>"There is a flower. And I think that she has tamed me"</em><br /><br />In each heart, lives a bunch of people who have loved us and whom we have loved. Through storm and sunshine, they will choose us again and again like they have before and we will choose them back. Because they are the ones we call our own, because they are the ones who have tamed us.<br /><br />And I guess, The Little Prince has tamed me as well.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8483837741465688502">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1220338562">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1220338562" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="left imgcol" title="Manny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" alt="Manny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1220338562?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="user" title="Manny">Manny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/67781.El_Principito" title="Paperback 9789500426404" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=linguistics-and-philosophy" class="actionLinkLite">linguistics-and-philosophy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=well-i-think-its-funny" class="actionLinkLite">well-i-think-its-funny</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=translation-is-impossible" class="actionLinkLite">translation-is-impossible</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=not-the-whole-truth" class="actionLinkLite">not-the-whole-truth</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=life-is-le-petit-prince" class="actionLinkLite">life-is-le-petit-prince</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=spanish" class="actionLinkLite">spanish</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1220338562">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1943424659340479345">We have visited Spain twice in the last year, and this time I decided that I really had to get better acquainted with the Spanish language. I knew that it was structurally very similar to French, but I had little vocabulary. I decided to try my usual first move: I went into a bookstore, bought a copy of <em>Le Petit Prince</em>, and opened it at page 1. <br /><br />Not, who fails to share my passion for language, was skeptical. If I more or less know this book by heart, she asked logically, in what sense am I readin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1943424659340479345">We have visited Spain twice in the last year, and this time I decided that I really had to get better acquainted with the Spanish language. I knew that it was structurally very similar to French, but I had little vocabulary. I decided to try my usual first move: I went into a bookstore, bought a copy of <em>Le Petit Prince</em>, and opened it at page 1. <br /><br />Not, who fails to share my passion for language, was skeptical. If I more or less know this book by heart, she asked logically, in what sense am I reading it? A perfectly good question; but what I'm doing, of course, is matching up the Spanish words and grammar to the text I can remember, and thereby increasing my command of Spanish. And it's worked quite well! In a couple of days, I have at least doubled my pitiful stock of words, and I'm starting to recognize the verb endings. Here's an example to show how far I've got. I give the Spanish original above and the sorta-French I am mentally filling in underneath:<br /><pre>—Señor —le dijo—, perdóneme si le pregunto...<br />-Sire -lui dit-(il)- pardonnez-moi si (je) vous interroge..<br /><br />— Te ordeno que me preguntes —se apresuró a decir el rey.<br />-(je) t' ordonne que (tu) m' interroges -s'est pressé à dire le roi.<br /><br />—Señor... ¿sobre qué ejerce su poder?<br />-Sire ... sur quoi éxercisez-(vous) votre pouvoir?<br /><br />—Sobre todo —contestó el rey con gran ingenuidad.<br />-Sur tout -répondait le roi avec grand ingenuité<br /><br />—¿Sobre todo?<br />- Sur tout?<br /><br />El rey, con un gesto sencillo, señaló su planeta, <br />Le roi, avec une geste ? , signalait sa planète, <br /><br />los otros planetas y las estrellas.<br />les autres planètes et les étoiles.</pre>So far, so good! I am now going to read the book a second time, and will then see how I do on something I'm not so familiar with...<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1943424659340479345">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20025931">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20025931" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/999233-laura" class="left imgcol" title="Laura"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1307313502p2/999233.jpg" alt="Laura" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20025931?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 25, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/999233-laura" class="user" title="Laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/157993.The_Little_Prince" title="Paperback 9780156012195" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=juvenile" class="actionLinkLite">juvenile</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=read-2008" class="actionLinkLite">read-2008</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=review-on-blog" class="actionLinkLite">review-on-blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20025931">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6582353510509454493">I read this book because I believed that it was a classic and that I would be missing out on something special, like The Phantom Tollbooth. This book was very bizarre, I couldn't get past its strangeness. The first couple of pages seemed fairly decent and I thought that I was going to be in for a treat. But then its shine wore off and I was wondering what was going on. The author left a lot of things unsaid and just went on with his random little monologue. <br /><br />I was annoyed because it had all the e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6582353510509454493">I read this book because I believed that it was a classic and that I would be missing out on something special, like The Phantom Tollbooth. This book was very bizarre, I couldn't get past its strangeness. The first couple of pages seemed fairly decent and I thought that I was going to be in for a treat. But then its shine wore off and I was wondering what was going on. The author left a lot of things unsaid and just went on with his random little monologue. <br /><br />I was annoyed because it had all the elements to be an interesting story, but it fell dreadfully short. Some parts of the book I thought were very insightful and I did like how easily the author could let you see things through a child's eyes. The way adults were portrayed was slightly rude, (you've got to give them more credit then that, not every adult is some mindless weirdo.) <br /><br />The ending was a bit of a shocker and I was not impressed, to me it gave off a totally bad feel and made it almost not a childrens book, it seemed dark and apathetic. I felt like the little prince did not know what he was doing and that the pilot should have stopped him. I did not make friends with the little prince and wasn't the least bit nostalgic at the end. I don't know why this book is hailed as a great classic. I didn't get much out of it and I know that I wouldn't recommend it to children, the ending was just not appropriate.<br /><br />*Taken from my book reviews blog: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008/06/book-review-128-little-prince-by.html" target="_blank">http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6582353510509454493">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1387189907">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14166710059206610479">La primera vez que lo leí fue a los 11 o 12 años. No había entendido muchas cosas y sobretodo el final. Una profesora mía me dijo que este es un libro que siempre hay que leerlo constantemente y le hice caso. En la mayoría de la historia pensé en la sociedad en la que estamos hoy en día y no ha cambiado mucho desde cuando Antoine escribió el libro, (75 años antes). Ahora que lo leí veo la otra cara de esta historia y el final me hizo derramar lágrimas y también darme cuenta que estamos todos con</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14166710059206610479">La primera vez que lo leí fue a los 11 o 12 años. No había entendido muchas cosas y sobretodo el final. Una profesora mía me dijo que este es un libro que siempre hay que leerlo constantemente y le hice caso. En la mayoría de la historia pensé en la sociedad en la que estamos hoy en día y no ha cambiado mucho desde cuando Antoine escribió el libro, (75 años antes). Ahora que lo leí veo la otra cara de esta historia y el final me hizo derramar lágrimas y también darme cuenta que estamos todos convertidos en adultos que sólo nos interesan las cifras. Simplemente el mejor de los clásicos.</span>
